When both skin test and RAST for BPO were negative , single - blind , placebo - controlled challenge tests were done to ensure tolerance of PG or sensitivity to AX . 
A total of 177 patients were diagnosed as <mark>allergic</mark> to beta - lactam antibiotics . 
We selected the 54 ( 30 . 5 % ) cases of immediate AX <mark>allergy</mark> with good tolerance of PG . 
<mark>Anaphylaxis</mark> was seen in 37 patients ( 69 % ) , the other 17 ( 31 % ) having <mark>urticaria</mark> and / or <mark>angioedema</mark> . 
All the patients were skin test negative to BPO ; 49 of 51 ( 96 % ) were also negative to <mark>MDM</mark> , and 44 of 46 ( 96 % ) to PG . 
Skin tests with AX were positive in 34 ( 63 % ) patients . 
RAST was positive for AX in 22 patients ( 41 % ) and to BPO in just 5 ( 9 % ) . 
None of the sera with negative RAST for AX were positive to BPO . 
Challenge tests with AX were performed in 23 subjects ( 43 % ) to establish the diagnosis of immediate <mark>allergic reaction</mark> to AX , and in 15 cases ( 28 % ) both skin test and RAST for AX were negative . 
PG was well tolerated by all 54 patients . 
We describe the largest group of AX - <mark>allergic</mark> patients who have tolerated PG reported so far . 
Diagnosis of these patients can be achieved only if specific AX - related reagents are employed . 
Further studies are necessary to determine the exact extent of this problem and to improve the efficacy of diagnostic methods . 
Reversal by phenylephrine of the beneficial effects of intravenous nitroglycerin in patients with <mark>acute myocardial infarction</mark> . 
Nitroglycerin has been shown to reduce ST - segment elevation during <mark>acute myocardial infarction</mark> , an effect potentiated in the dog by agents that reverse nitroglycerin - induced <mark>hypotension</mark> . 
Our study was designed to determine the effects of combined nitroglycerin and phenylephrine therapy . 
Ten patients with acute transmural <mark>myocardial infarctions</mark> received intravenous nitroglycerin , sufficient to reduce mean arterial pressure from 107 + / - 6 to 85 + / - 6 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 001 ) , for 60 minutes . 
Left ventricular filling pressure decreased from 19 + / - 2 to 11 + / - 2 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 001 ) . 
SigmaST , the sum of ST - segment elevations in 16 precordial leads , decreased ( P less than 0 . 02 ) with intravenous nitroglycerin . 
Subsequent addition of phenylephrine infusion , sufficient to re - elevate mean arterial pressure to 106 + / - 4 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 001 ) for 30 minutes , increased left ventricular filling pressure to 17 + / - 2 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 05 ) and also significantly increased sigmaST ( P less than 0 . 05 ) . 
Our results suggest that addition of phenylephrine to nitroglycerin is not beneficial in the treatment of patients with <mark>acute myocardial infarction</mark> . 
Acetazolamide - induced <mark>nephrolithiasis</mark> : implications for treatment of <mark>neuromuscular disorders</mark> . 
Carbonic anhydrase inhibitors can cause <mark>nephrolithiasis</mark> . 
We studied 20 patients receiving long - term carbonic anhydrase inhibitor treatment for periodic <mark>paralysis</mark> and <mark>myotonia</mark> . 
Three patients on acetazolamide ( 15 % ) developed <mark>renal calculi</mark> . 
Extracorporeal lithotripsy successfully removed a <mark>renal calculus</mark> in one patient and surgery removed a staghorn <mark>calculus</mark> in another , permitting continued treatment . 
Renal function remained normal in all patients . 
<mark>Nephrolithiasis</mark> is a complication of acetazolamide but does not preclude its use . 
Effects of calcium channel blockers on bupivacaine - induced <mark>toxicity</mark> . 
The purpose of this study was to investigate the influence of calcium channel blockers on bupivacaine - induced acute <mark>toxicity</mark> . 
For each of the three tested calcium channel blockers ( diltiazem , verapamil and bepridil ) 6 groups of mice were treated by two different doses , i . e . 2 and 10 mg / kg / i . p . , or an equal volume of saline for the control group ( n = 20 ) ; 15 minutes later , all the animals were injected with a single 50 mg / kg / i . p . dose of bupivacaine . 
The convulsant activity , the time of latency to convulse and the mortality rate were assessed in each group . 
The local anesthetic - induced mortality was significantly increased by the three different calcium channel blockers . 
The convulsant activity of bupivacaine was not significantly modified but calcium channel blockers decreased the time of latency to obtain bupivacaine - induced <mark>convulsions</mark> ; this effect was less pronounced with bepridil . 
Epidural blood flow during prostaglandin E1 or trimethaphan induced <mark>hypotension</mark> . 
To evaluate the effect of prostaglandin E1 ( PGE1 ) or trimethaphan ( TMP ) induced <mark>hypotension</mark> on epidural blood flow ( EBF ) during spinal surgery , EBF was measured using the heat clearance method in 30 patients who underwent postero - lateral interbody fusion under isoflurane anaesthesia . 
An initial dose of 0 . 1 microgram . kg - 1 . min - 1 of PGE1 ( 15 patients ) , or 10 micrograms . kg - 1 . min - 1 of TMP ( 15 patients ) was administered intravenously after the dural opening and the dose was adjusted to maintain the mean arterial blood pressure ( MAP ) at about 60 mmHg . 
The <mark>hypotensive</mark> drug was discontinued at the completion of the operative procedure . 
After starting PGE1 or TMP , MAP and rate pressure product ( RPP ) decreased significantly compared with preinfusion values ( P < 0 . 01 ) , and the degree of <mark>hypotension</mark> due to PGE1 remained constant until 60 min after its discontinuation . 
Heart rate ( HR ) did not change in either group . 
EBFF did not change during PGE1 infusion whereas in the TMP group , EBF decreased significantly at 30 and 60 min after the start of TMP ( preinfusion : 45 . 9 + / - 13 . 9 ml / 100g / min . 30 min : 32 . 3 + / - 9 . 9 ml / 100 g / min ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 60 min : 30 + / - 7 . 5 ml / 100 g / min ( P < 0 . 05 ) ) . 
These results suggest that PGE1 may be preferable to TMP for <mark>hypotensive</mark> anaesthesia in spinal surgery because TMP decreased EBF . 
Dup 753 prevents the development of puromycin aminonucleoside - induced <mark>nephrosis</mark> . 
The appearance of <mark>nephrotic syndromes</mark> such as <mark>proteinuria</mark> , <mark>hypoalbuminemia</mark> , <mark>hypercholesterolemia</mark> and increase in blood nitrogen urea , induced in rats by injection of puromycin aminonucleoside was markedly inhibited by oral administration of Dup 753 ( losartan ) , a novel angiotensin II receptor antagonist , at a dose of 1 or 2 mg / kg per day . 
The results suggest a possible involvement of the renin - angiotensin system in the development of puromycin aminonucleoside - induced <mark>nephrosis</mark> . 
Neuroplasticity of the adult primate auditory cortex following cochlear <mark>hearing loss</mark> . 
Tonotopic organization is an essential feature of the primary auditory area ( A1 ) of primate cortex . 
In A1 of macaque monkeys , low frequencies are represented rostrolaterally and high frequencies are represented caudomedially . 
The purpose of this study was to determine if changes occur in this tonotopic organization following cochlear <mark>hearing loss</mark> . 
Under anesthesia , the superior temporal gyrus of adult macaque monkeys was exposed , and the tonotopic organization of A1 was mapped using conventional microelectrode recording techniques . 
Following recovery , the monkeys were selectively deafened for high frequencies using kanamycin and furosemide . 
The actual frequencies deafened were determined by the loss of tone - burst elicited auditory brainstem responses . 
Three months after deafening , A1 was remapped . 
Postmortem cytoarchitectural features identifying A1 were correlated with the electrophysiologic data . 
The results indicate that the deprived area of A1 undergoes extensive reorganization and becomes responsive to intact cochlear frequencies . 
The region of cortex that represents the low frequencies was not obviously affected by the cochlear <mark>hearing loss</mark> . 
Sodium bicarbonate alleviates <mark>penile pain</mark> induced by intracavernous injections for <mark>erectile dysfunction</mark> . 
In an attempt to determine whether <mark>penile pain</mark> associated with intracorporeal injections could be due to the acidity of the medication , we performed a randomized study comparing the incidence of <mark>penile pain</mark> following intracorporeal injections with or without the addition of sodium bicarbonate to the intracorporeal medications . 
A total of 38 consecutive patients who presented to our clinic with <mark>impotence</mark> received 0 . 2 ml . of a combination of 3 drugs : 6 mg . papaverine , 100 micrograms . phentolamine and 10 micrograms . prostaglandin E1 with ( pH 7 . 05 ) or without ( pH 4 . 17 ) the addition of sodium bicarbonate ( 0 . 03 mEq . ) . 
Of the 19 patients without sodium bicarbonate added to the medication 11 ( 58 % ) complained of <mark>penile pain</mark> due to the medication , while only 1 of the 19 men ( 5 % ) who received sodium bicarbonate complained of <mark>penile pain</mark> . 
From these data we conclude that the <mark>penile pain</mark> following intracorporeal injections is most likely due to the acidity of the medication , which can be overcome by elevating the pH to a neutral level . 
The use and <mark>toxicity</mark> of didanosine ( ddI ) in <mark>HIV antibody - positive</mark> individuals intolerant to zidovudine ( AZT ) 
One hundred and fifty - one patients intolerant to zidovudine ( AZT ) received didanosine ( ddI ) to a maximum dose of 12 . 5 mg / kg / day . 
Patient response was assessed using changes in CD4 + lymphocyte subset count , HIV p24 antigen , weight , and quality of life . 
Seventy patients developed major <mark>opportunistic infections</mark> whilst on therapy ; this was the first <mark>AIDS</mark> diagnosis in 17 . 
Only minor changes in CD4 + lymphocyte subset count were observed in <mark>AIDS</mark> patients , although a more significant rise occurred in those with earlier stages of disease . 
Of those positive for p24 antigen at the commencement of the study 67 % showed a positive response , and this was most likely in those with CD4 + lymphocyte subset counts above 100 mm3 . 
A positive weight response was seen in 16 % of patients . 
Most patients showed improvement in individual parameters and global score of quality of life . 
Adverse reactions possibly attributable to didanosine were common . 
The most common side - effect was <mark>diarrhoea</mark> , which resulted in cessation of therapy in 19 individuals . 
<mark>Peripheral neuropathy</mark> occurred in 12 patients and <mark>pancreatitis</mark> in six . 
Thirteen patients developed a raised serum amylase without <mark>abdominal pain</mark> . 
Seven patients developed <mark>glucose tolerance curves</mark> characteristic of <mark>diabetes</mark> but these were mild , did not require treatment and returned to normal on ceasing didanosine . 
Immunohistochemical studies with antibodies to neurofilament proteins on <mark>axonal damage</mark> in experimental focal lesions in rat . 
Immunohistochemistry with monoclonal antibodies against neurofilament ( NF ) proteins of middle and high molecular weight class , NF - M and NF - H , was used to study <mark>axonal injury</mark> in the borderzone of focal lesions in rats . 
Focal <mark>injury in the cortex</mark> was produced by infusion of lactate at acid pH or by stab caused by needle insertion . 
<mark>Infarcts in substantia nigra pars reticulata</mark> were evoked by prolonged pilocarpine - induced <mark>status epilepticus</mark> . 
Immunohistochemical staining for NFs showed characteristic terminal clubs of axons in the borderzone of lesions . 
Differences in the labelling pattern occurred with different antibodies which apparently depended on molecular weight class of NFs and phosphorylation state . 
These immunohistochemical changes of NFs can serve as a marker for <mark>axonal damage</mark> in various experimental <mark>traumatic</mark> or ischemic lesions . 
Pharmacokinetic and clinical studies in patients with cimetidine - associated mental <mark>confusion</mark> . 
15 cases of cimetidine - associated mental <mark>confusion</mark> have been reported . 
In order that this syndrome might be investigated changes in mental status ( M . S . ) were correlated with serum concentrations and renal and hepatic function in 36 patients , 30 patients had no M . S . change on cimetidine and 6 had moderate to severe changes . 
These 6 patients had both <mark>renal and liver dysfunction</mark> ( P less than 0 . 05 ) , as well as cimetidine trough - concentrations of more than 1 . 25 microgram / ml ( P less than 0 . 05 ) . 
The severity of M . S . changes increased as trough - concentrations rose , 5 patients had lumbar puncture . 
The cerebrospinal fluid : serum ratio of cimetidine concentrations was 0 . 24 : 1 and indicates that cimetidine passes the blood - brain barrier ; it also raises the possibility that M . S . changes are due to blockade of histamine H2 - receptors in the central nervous system . 
Patients likely to have both raised trough - concentrations and mental <mark>confusion</mark> are those with both severe <mark>renal and hepatic dysfunction</mark> . 
They should be closely observed and should be given reduced doses of cimetidine . 
Prospective study of the long - term effects of somatostatin analog ( octreotide ) on gallbladder function and <mark>gallstone</mark> formation in Chinese <mark>acromegalic</mark> patients . 
This article reports the changes in gallbladder function examined by ultrasonography in 20 Chinese patients with active <mark>acromegaly</mark> treated with sc injection of the somatostatin analog octreotide in dosages of 300 - 1500 micrograms / day for a mean of 24 . 2 + / - 13 . 9 months . 
During treatment with octreotide , 17 patients developed sludge , 10 had <mark>gallstones</mark> , and 1 developed <mark>acute cholecystitis</mark> requiring surgery . 
In all of 7 patients examined acutely , gallbladder contractility was inhibited after a single 100 - micrograms injection . 
In 8 patients followed for 24 weeks , gallbladder contractility remained <mark>depressed</mark> throughout therapy . 
After withdrawal of octreotide in 10 patients without <mark>gallstones</mark> , 8 patients assessed had return of normal gallbladder contractility within 1 month . 
In 8 of the remaining 10 patients who developed <mark>gallstones</mark> during treatment , gallbladder contractility normalized in 5 patients ( 3 of whom has disappearance of their stones within 3 weeks ) , and remained <mark>depressed</mark> in 3 ( 2 of whom had stones present at 6 months ) . 
Our results suggest that the suppression of gallbladder contractility is the cause of the successive formation of bile sludge , <mark>gallstones</mark> , and <mark>cholecystitis</mark> during octreotide therapy in Chinese <mark>acromegalic</mark> patients . 
It is therefore very important to follow the changes of gallbladder function during long - term octreotide therapy of <mark>acromegalic</mark> patients . 
Increase of <mark>Parkinson disability</mark> after fluoxetine medication . 
<mark>Depression</mark> is a major clinical feature of <mark>Parkinson ' s disease</mark> . 
We report the increased amount of <mark>motor disability</mark> in four patients with <mark>idiopathic Parkinson ' s disease</mark> after exposure to the antidepressant fluoxetine . 
The possibility of a clinically relevant dopamine - antagonistic capacity of fluoxetine in <mark>Parkinson ' s disease</mark> patients must be considered . 
<mark>Sinus arrest</mark> associated with continuous - infusion cimetidine . 
The administration of intermittent intravenous infusions of cimetidine is infrequently associated with the development of <mark>bradyarrhythmias</mark> . 
A 40 - year - old man with <mark>leukemia</mark> and no history of <mark>cardiac disease</mark> developed recurrent , brief episodes of apparent <mark>sinus arrest</mark> while receiving continuous - infusion cimetidine 50 mg / hour . 
The <mark>arrhythmias</mark> were temporally related to cimetidine administration , disappeared after dechallenge , and did not recur during ranitidine treatment . 
This is the first reported case of <mark>sinus arrest</mark> associated with continuous - infusion cimetidine . 
Phase II trial of vinorelbine in metastatic <mark>squamous cell esophageal carcinoma</mark> . 
European Organization for Research and Treatment of <mark>Cancer</mark> Gastrointestinal Treat <mark>Cancer</mark> Cooperative Group . 
PURPOSE : To evaluate the response rate and toxic effects of vinorelbine ( VNB ) administered as a single agent in metastatic <mark>squamous cell esophageal carcinoma</mark> . 
PATIENTS AND METHODS : Forty - six eligible patients with measurable lesions were included and were stratified according to previous chemotherapy . 
Thirty patients without prior chemotherapy and 16 pretreated with cisplatin - based chemotherapy were assessable for <mark>toxicity</mark> and response . 
VNB was administered weekly as a 25 - mg / m2 short intravenous ( i . v . ) infusion . 
RESULTS : Six of 30 patients ( 20 % ) without prior chemotherapy achieved a partial response ( PR ) ( 95 % confidence interval [ CI ] , 8 % to 39 % ) . 
The median duration of response was 21 weeks ( range , 17 to 28 ) . 
One of 16 patients ( 6 % ) with prior chemotherapy had a complete response ( CR ) of 31 weeks ' duration ( 95 % CI , 0 % to 30 % ) . 
The overall response rate ( World Health Organization [ WHO ] criteria ) was 15 % ( CR , 2 % ; PR 13 % ; 95 % CI , 6 % to 29 % ) . 
The median dose - intensity ( DI ) was 20 mg / m2 / wk . 
VNB was well tolerated and zero instances of WHO grade 4 nonhematologic <mark>toxicity</mark> occurred . 
At least one episode of grade 3 or 4 <mark>granulocytopenia</mark> was seen in 59 % of patients . 
A grade 2 or 3 <mark>infection</mark> occurred in 16 % of patients , but no toxic <mark>deaths</mark> occurred . 
Other side effects were rare , and <mark>peripheral neurotoxicity</mark> has been minor ( 26 % grade 1 ) . 
CONCLUSION : These data indicate that VNB is an active agent in metastatic <mark>esophageal squamous cell carcinoma</mark> . 
Given its excellent tolerance profile and low <mark>toxicity</mark> , further evaluation of VNB in combination therapy is warranted . 
Evaluation of adverse reactions of aponidine hydrochloride ophthalmic solution . 
We prospectively evaluated the adverse reactions of apraclonidine in 20 normal volunteers by instilling a single drop of 1 % apraclonidine in their right eyes . 
Examinations , including blood pressure , pulse rate , conjunctiva and cornea , intraocular pressure ( IOP ) , pupil diameter , basal tear secretion and margin reflex distance of both upper and lower eyelids , were performed prior to entry and at 1 , 3 , 5 and 7 hours after instillation . 
The <mark>ocular hypotensive</mark> effects were statistically significant for apraclonidine - treated eyes throughout the study and also statistically significant for contralateral eyes from three hours after topical administration of 1 % apraclonidine . 
<mark>Decreases in systolic blood pressure</mark> were statistically , but not clinically , significant . 
No significant changes in diastolic blood pressure , pulse rate and basal tear secretion were noted . 
<mark>Conjunctival blanching</mark> and <mark>mydriasis</mark> were commonly found . 
Upper lid retraction was frequently noted . 
While the elevations of the upper lid margin in most subjects were not more than 2 mm and did not cause noticeable change in appearance , one subject suffered from mechanical <mark>entropion</mark> and marked <mark>corneal abrasion</mark> 3 hours after instillation of the medication . 
This may well be a particularly notable finding in Asian people . 
Thiopentone pretreatment for propofol injection <mark>pain</mark> in ambulatory patients . 
This study investigated propofol injection <mark>pain</mark> in patients undergoing ambulatory anaesthesia . 
In a randomized , double - blind trial , 90 women were allocated to receive one of three treatments prior to induction of anaesthesia with propofol . 
Patients in Group C received 2 ml normal saline , Group L , 2 ml , lidocaine 2 % ( 40 mg ) and Group T , 2 ml thiopentone 2 . 5 % ( 50 mg ) . 
Venous discomfort was assessed with a visual analogue scale ( VAS ) 5 - 15 sec after commencing propofol administration using an infusion pump ( rate 1000 micrograms . kg - 1 . min - 1 ) . 
<mark>Loss of consciousness</mark> occurred in 60 - 90 sec . 
Visual analogue scores ( mean + / - SD ) during induction were lower in Groups L ( 3 . 3 + / - 2 . 5 ) and T ( 4 . 1 + / - 2 . 7 ) than in Group C ( 5 . 6 + / - 2 . 3 ) ; P = 0 . 0031 . 
The incidence of venous discomfort was lower in Group L ( 76 . 6 % ; P < 0 . 05 ) than in Group C ( 100 % ) but not different from Group T ( 90 % ) . 
The VAS scores for recall of <mark>pain</mark> in the recovery room were correlated with the VAS scores during induction ( r = 0 . 7045 ; P < 0 . 0001 ) . 
Recovery room discharge times were similar : C ( 75 . 9 + / - 19 . 4 min ) ; L 73 . 6 + / - 21 . 6 min ) ; T ( 77 . 1 + / - 18 . 9 min ) . 
Assessing their overall satisfaction , 89 . 7 % would choose propofol anaesthesia again . 
We conclude that lidocaine reduces the incidence and severity of propofol injection <mark>pain</mark> in ambulatory patients whereas thiopentone only reduces its severity . 
Persistent <mark>paralysis</mark> after prolonged use of atracurium in the absence of corticosteroids . 
Neuromuscular blocking agents ( NMBAs ) are often used for patients requiring prolonged mechanical ventilation . 
Reports of persistent <mark>paralysis</mark> after the discontinuance of these drugs have most often involved aminosteroid - based NMBAs such as vecuronium bromide , especially when used in conjunction with corticosteroids . 
Atracurium besylate , a short - acting benzylisoquinolinium NMBA that is eliminated independently of renal or hepatic function , has also been associated with persistent <mark>paralysis</mark> , but only when used with corticosteroids . 
We report a case of atracurium - related <mark>paralysis</mark> persisting for approximately 50 hours in a patient who was not treated with corticosteroids . 
A phase I / II study of paclitaxel plus cisplatin as first - line therapy for <mark>head and neck cancers</mark> : preliminary results . 
Improved outcomes among patients with <mark>head and neck carcinomas</mark> require investigations of new drugs for induction therapy . 
Preliminary results of an Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group study of single - agent paclitaxel ( Taxol ; Bristol - Myers Squibb Company , Princeton , NJ ) reported a 37 % response rate in patients with <mark>head and neck cancer</mark> , and the paclitaxel / cisplatin combination has been used successfully and has significantly improved median response duration in <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> patients . 
We initiated a phase I / II trial to determine the response and <mark>toxicity</mark> of escalating paclitaxel doses combined with fixed - dose cisplatin with granulocyte colony - stimulating factor support in patients with untreated locally advanced inoperable <mark>head and neck carcinoma</mark> . 
To date , 23 men with a median age of 50 years and good performance status have entered the trial . 
Primary <mark>tumor</mark> sites were oropharynx , 10 patients ; hypopharynx , four ; larynx , two ; oral cavity , three ; unknown primary , two ; and nasal cavity and parotid gland , one each . 
Of 20 patients evaluable for <mark>toxicity</mark> , four had stage III and 16 had stage IV disease . 
Treatment , given every 21 days for a maximum of three cycles , consisted of paclitaxel by 3 - hour infusion followed the next day by a fixed dose of cisplatin ( 75 mg / m2 ) . 
The dose levels incorporate escalating paclitaxel doses , and intrapatient escalations within a given dose level are permitted if <mark>toxicity</mark> permits . 
At the time of this writing , dose level 4 ( 260 , 270 , and 280 mg / m2 ) is being evaluated ; three patients from this level are evaluable . 
With paclitaxel doses of 200 mg / m2 and higher , granulocyte colony - stimulating factor 5 micrograms / kg / d is given ( days 4 through 12 ) . 
Of 18 patients evaluable for response , seven ( 39 % ) achieved a complete response and six ( 33 % ) achieved a partial response . 
Three patients had no change and disease progressed in two . 
The overall response rate is 72 % . 
Eleven responding patients had subsequent surgery / radiotherapy or radical radiotherapy . 
Two pathologic complete responses were observed in patients who had achieved clinical complete responses . 
<mark>Alopecia</mark> , <mark>paresthesias</mark> , and <mark>arthralgias</mark> / <mark>myalgias</mark> have occurred frequently , but with one exception ( a grade 3 <mark>myalgia</mark> ) they have been grade 1 or 2 . 
No dose - limiting hematologic <mark>toxicity</mark> has been seen . 
Paclitaxel / cisplatin is an effective first - line regimen for locoregionally advanced <mark>head and neck cancer</mark> and continued study is warranted . 
Results thus far suggest no dose - response effect for paclitaxel doses above 200 mg / m2 . 
Improvement of levodopa - induced <mark>dyskinesia</mark> by propranolol in <mark>Parkinson ' s disease</mark> . 
Seven patients suffering from <mark>Parkinson ' s disease</mark> ( <mark>PD</mark> ) with severely disabling <mark>dyskinesia</mark> received low - dose propranolol as an adjunct to the currently used medical treatment . 
There was a significant 40 % improvement in the <mark>dyskinesia</mark> score without increase of <mark>parkinsonian</mark> <mark>motor disability</mark> . 
Ballistic and choreic <mark>dyskinesia</mark> were markedly ameliorated , whereas <mark>dystonia</mark> was not . 
This study suggests that administration of low doses of beta - blockers may improve levodopa - induced ballistic and choreic <mark>dyskinesia</mark> in <mark>PD</mark> . 
Habitual use of acetaminophen as a risk factor for <mark>chronic renal failure</mark> : a comparison with phenacetin . 
Six epidemiologic studies in the United States and Europe indicate that habitual use of phenacetin is associated with the development of <mark>chronic renal failure</mark> and <mark>end - stage renal disease</mark> ( <mark>ESRD</mark> ) , with a relative risk in the range of 4 to 19 . 
As a result of these and other studies , phenacetin has now been withdrawn from the market in most countries . 
However , three case control studies , one each in North Carolina , northern Maryland , and West Berlin , Germany , showed that habitual use of acetaminophen is also associated with <mark>chronic renal failure</mark> and <mark>ESRD</mark> , with a relative risk in the range of 2 to 4 . 
These studies suggest that both phenacetin and acetaminophen may contribute to the burden of <mark>ESRD</mark> , with the risk of the latter being somewhat less than that of the former . 
This apparent difference in risk may not be due to differences in <mark>nephrotoxic</mark> potential of the drugs themselves . 
A lower relative risk would be expected for acetaminophen if the risk of both drugs in combination with other analgesics was higher than the risk of either agent alone . 
Thus , acetaminophen has been used both as a single agent and in combination with other analgesics , whereas phenacetin was available only in combinations . 
The possibility that habitual use of acetaminophen alone increases the risk of <mark>ESRD</mark> has not been clearly demonstrated , but cannot be dismissed . 
Acetaminophen - induced <mark>hypotension</mark> . 
Through 30 years of widespread use , acetaminophen has been shown to be a remarkably safe medication in therapeutic dosages . 
The potential for acetaminophen to produce <mark>cardiovascular toxicities</mark> is very low . 
However , acetaminophen has been demonstrated to produce symptoms of <mark>anaphylaxis</mark> , including <mark>hypotension</mark> , in sensitive individuals . 
This article describes two <mark>critically ill</mark> patients in whom transient episodes of <mark>hypotension</mark> reproducibly developed after administration of acetaminophen . 
Other symptoms of <mark>allergic reactions</mark> were not clinically detectable . 
The <mark>hypotensive</mark> episodes were severe enough to require vasopressor administration . 
The reports illustrate the need for clinicians to consider acetaminophen in patients with <mark>hypotension</mark> of unknown origin . 
Reduction of heparan sulphate - associated anionic sites in the glomerular basement membrane of rats with streptozotocin - induced <mark>diabetic nephropathy</mark> . 
Heparan sulphate - associated anionic sites in the glomerular basement membrane were studied in rats 8 months after induction of <mark>diabetes</mark> by streptozotocin and in age - adn sex - matched control rats , employing the cationic dye cuprolinic blue . 
Morphometric analysis at the ultrastructural level was performed using a computerized image processor . 
The heparan sulphate specificity of the cuprolinic blue staining was demonstrated by glycosaminoglycan - degrading enzymes , showing that pretreatment of the sections with heparitinase abolished all staining , whereas chondroitinase ABC had no effect . 
The majority of anionic sites ( 74 % in <mark>diabetic</mark> and 81 % in control rats ) were found within the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane . 
A minority of anionic sites were scattered throughout the lamina densa and lamina rara interna , and were significantly smaller than those in the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane ( p < 0 . 001 and p < 0 . 01 for <mark>diabetic</mark> and control rats , respectively ) . 
<mark>Diabetic</mark> rats progressively developed <mark>albuminuria</mark> reaching 40 . 3 ( 32 . 2 - 62 . 0 ) mg / 24 h after 8 months in contrast to the control animals ( 0 . 8 ( 0 . 2 - 0 . 9 ) mg / 24 h , p < 0 . 002 ) . 
At the same time , the number of heparan sulphate anionic sites and the total anionic site surface ( number of anionic sites x mean anionic site surface ) in the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane was reduced by 19 % ( p < 0 . 021 ) and by 26 % ( p < 0 . 02 ) , respectively . 
Number and total anionic site surface in the remaining part of the glomerular basement membrane ( lamina densa and lamina rara interna ) were not significantly changed . 
We conclude that in streptozotocin - <mark>diabetic</mark> rats with an increased urinary albumin excretion , a reduced heparan sulphate charge barrier / density is found at the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane . 
Mediation of enhanced reflex vagal <mark>bradycardia</mark> by L - dopa via central dopamine formation in dogs . 
L - Dopa ( 5 mg / kg i . v . ) decreased blood pressure and heart rate after extracerebral decarboxylase inhibition with MK - 486 ( 25 mg / kg i . v . ) in anesthetize MAO - inhibited dogs . 
In addition , reflex <mark>bradycardia</mark> caused by injected norepinephrine was significantly enhanced by L - dopa , DL - Threo - dihydroxyphenylserine had no effect on blood pressure , heart rate or reflex responses to norepinephrine . 
FLA - 63 , a dopamine - beta - oxidase inhibitor , did not have any effect on the <mark>hypotension</mark> , <mark>bradycardia</mark> or reflex - enhancing effect of L - dopa . 
Pimozide did not affect the actions of L - dopa on blood pressure and heart rate but completely blocked the enhancement of reflexes . 
Removal of the carotid sinuses caused an elevation blood pressure and heart rate and abolished the negative chronotropic effect of norepinephrine . 
However , L - dopa restored the <mark>bradycardia</mark> caused by norepinephrine in addition to decreasing blood pressure and heart rate . 
5 - HTP ( 5 mg / kg i . v . ) decreased blood pressure and heart rate and decreased the reflex <mark>bradycardia</mark> to norepinephrine . 
It is concluded that L - dopa enhances reflex <mark>bradycardia</mark> through central alpha - receptor stimulation . 
Furthermore , the effects are mediated through dopamine rather than norepinephrine and do not require the carotid sinus baroreceptors . 
<mark>Microangiopathic hemolytic anemia</mark> complicating FK506 ( tacrolimus ) therapy . 
We describe 3 episodes of <mark>microangiopathic hemolytic anemia</mark> ( <mark>MAHA</mark> ) in 2 solid organ recipients under FK506 ( tacrolimus ) therapy . 
In both cases , discontinuation of FK506 and treatment with plasma exchange , fresh frozen plasma replacement , corticosteroids , aspirin , and dipyridamole led to resolution of <mark>MAHA</mark> . 
In one patient , reintroduction of FK506 led to rapid recurrence of <mark>MAHA</mark> . 
FK506 - associated <mark>MAHA</mark> is probably rare but physicians must be aware of this severe complication . 
In our experience and according to the literature , FK506 does not seem to cross - react with cyclosporin A ( CyA ) , an immuno - suppressive drug already known to induce <mark>MAHA</mark> . 
Effect of some anticancer drugs and combined chemotherapy on <mark>renal toxicity</mark> . 
The <mark>nephrotoxic</mark> action of anticancer drugs such as nitrogranulogen ( NG ) , methotrexate ( MTX ) , 5 - fluorouracil ( 5 - FU ) and cyclophosphamide ( CY ) administered alone or in combination [ MTX + 5 - FU + CY ( CMF ) ] was evaluated in experiments on Wistar rats . 
After drug administration , creatinine concentrations in the plasma and in the urine of the rats were determined , as well as creatinine clearance . 
Histopathologic evaluation of the kidneys was also performed . 
After MTX administration a significant increase ( p = 0 . 0228 ) in the plasma creatinine concentration and a significant ( p = 0 . 0001 ) decrease in creatinine clearance was noted compared to controls . 
After the administration of NG , 5 - FU and CY neither a statistically significant increase in creatinine concentration nor an increase in creatinine clearance was observed compared to the group receiving no cytostatics . 
Following polytherapy according to the CMF regimen , a statistically significant decrease ( p = 0 . 0343 ) in creatinine clearance was found , but creatinine concentration did not increase significantly compared to controls . 
CY caused <mark>hemorrhagic cystitis</mark> in 40 % of rats , but it did not cause this complication when combined with 5 - FU and MTX . 
Histologic changes were found in rat kidneys after administration of MTX , CY and NG , while no such change was observed after 5 - FU and joint administration of MTX + 5 - FU + CY compared to controls . 
Our studies indicate that <mark>nephrotoxicity</mark> of MTX + 5 - FU + CY administered jointly is lower than in monotherapy . 
The interpeduncular nucleus regulates nicotine ' s effects on free - field activity . 
Partial lesions were made with kainic acid in the interpeduncular nucleus of the ventral midbrain of the rat . 
Compared with sham - operated controls , lesions significantly ( p < 0 . 25 ) blunted the early ( < 60 min ) free - field <mark>locomotor hypoactivity</mark> caused by nicotine ( 0 . 5 mg kg ( - 1 ) , i . m . ) , enhanced the later ( 60 - 120 min ) nicotine - induced <mark>hyperactivity</mark> , and raised spontaneous nocturnal activity . 
Lesions reduced the extent of immunohistological staining for choline acetyltransferase in the interpeduncular nucleus ( p < 0 . 025 ) , but not for tyrosine hydroxylase in the surrounding catecholaminergic A10 region . 
We conclude that the interpeduncular nucleus mediates nicotinic <mark>depression</mark> of locomotor activity and dampens nicotinic arousal mechanisms located elsewhere in the brain . 
Lithium - associated <mark>cognitive and functional deficits</mark> reduced by a switch to divalproex sodium : a case series . 
BACKGROUND : Lithium remains a first - line treatment for the acute and maintenance treatment of <mark>bipolar disorder</mark> . 
Although much has been written about the management of the more common adverse effects of lithium , such as <mark>polyuria</mark> and <mark>tremor</mark> , more subtle lithium side effects such as <mark>cognitive deficits</mark> , <mark>loss of creativity</mark> , and <mark>functional impairments</mark> remain understudied . 
This report summarizes our experience in switching <mark>bipolar</mark> patients from lithium to divalproex sodium to alleviate such <mark>cognitive and functional impairments</mark> . 
METHOD : Open , case series design . 
RESULTS : We report seven cases where substitution of lithium , either fully or partially , with divalproex sodium was extremely helpful in reducing the <mark>cognitive , motivational , or creative deficits</mark> attributed to lithium in our <mark>bipolar</mark> patients . 
CONCLUSION : In this preliminary report , divalproex sodium was a superior alternative to lithium in <mark>bipolar</mark> patients experiencing <mark>cognitive deficits</mark> , <mark>loss of creativity</mark> , and <mark>functional impairments</mark> . 
Effect of nifedipine on renal function in liver transplant recipients receiving tacrolimus . 
The effect of nifedipine on renal function in liver transplant recipients who were receiving tacrolimus was evaluated between January 1992 and January 1996 . 
Two groups of patients receiving tacrolimus were compared over a period of 1 year , one group comprising <mark>hypertensive</mark> patients who were receiving nifedipine , and the other comprising nonhypertensive patients not receiving nifedipine . 
The time from transplant to baseline was similar in all patients . 
Nifedipine significantly improved kidney function as indicated by a significant lowering of serum creatinine levels at 6 and 12 months . 
The observed positive impact of nifedipine on reducing the <mark>nephrotoxicity</mark> associated with tacrolimus in liver transplant recipients should be an important factor in selecting an agent to treat <mark>hypertension</mark> in this population . 
Alpha and beta <mark>coma</mark> in drug intoxication uncomplicated by <mark>cerebral hypoxia</mark> . 
Four patients who were rendered <mark>comatose</mark> or <mark>stuporous</mark> by drug intoxication , but who were not hypoxic , are described . 
Three patients received high doses of chlormethiazole for alcohol <mark>withdrawal symptoms</mark> , and one took a suicidal <mark>overdose</mark> of nitrazepam . 
The patient with nitrazepam <mark>overdose</mark> and two of those with chlormethiazole intoxication conformed to the criteria of ' alpha <mark>coma</mark> ' , showing non - reactive generalized or frontally predominant alpha activity in the EEG . 
The fourth patient who was unconscious after chlormethiazole administration exhibite generalized non - reactive activity in the slow beta range . 
All four recovered completely without <mark>neurological sequelae</mark> following the withdrawal of the offending agents . 
The similarities between the effects of structural lesions and pharmacological <mark>depression</mark> of the brain stem reticular formation are discussed . 
It is suggested that in both situations disturbed reticulo - thalamic interactions are important in the pathogenesis of alpha <mark>coma</mark> . 
It is concluded that when this electroencephalographic and behavioural picture is seen in drug intoxication , in the absence of significant <mark>hypoxaemia</mark> , a favourable outcome may be anticipated . 
Magnetic resonance volumetry of the cerebellum in <mark>epileptic</mark> patients after phenytoin <mark>overdosages</mark> . 
The aim of this study was to evaluate the relationship between phenytoin medication and <mark>cerebellar atrophy</mark> in patients who had experienced clinical intoxication . 
Five females and 6 males , 21 - 59 years of age , were examined with a 1 . 5 - T whole - body system using a circular polarized head coil . 
Conventional spin echo images were acquired in the sagittal and transverse orientation . 
In addition , we performed a high - resolution 3D gradient echo , T1 - weighted sequences at a 1 - mm slice thickness . 
The images were subsequently processed to obtain volumetric data for the cerebellum . 
Cerebellar volume for the patient group ranged between 67 . 66 and 131 . 08 ml ( mean 108 . 9 ml ) . 
In addition 3D gradient echo data sets from 10 healthy male and 10 healthy female age - matched volunteers were used to compare cerebellar volumes . 
Using linear regression we found that no correlation exists between <mark>seizure</mark> duration , elevation of phenytoin serum levels and cerebellar volume . 
However , multiple regression for the daily dosage , duration of phenytoin treatment and cerebellar volume revealed a correlation of these parameters . 
We conclude that phenytoin <mark>overdosage</mark> does not necessarily result in <mark>cerebellar atrophy</mark> and it is unlikely that phenytoin medication was the only cause of <mark>cerebellar atrophy</mark> in the remaining patients . 
Quantitative morphometric studies of the cerebellum provide valuable insights into the pathogenesis of <mark>cerebellar disorders</mark> . 
Late recovery of renal function in a woman with the <mark>hemolytic uremic syndrome</mark> . 
A case is reported of the <mark>hemolytic uremic syndrome</mark> ( <mark>HUS</mark> ) in a woman taking oral contraceptives . 
She was treated with heparin , dipyridamole and hemodialysis ; and after more than three months , her urinary output rose above 500 ml ; and six months after the onset of <mark>anuria</mark> , dialysis treatment was stopped . 
This case emphasizes the possibility that <mark>HUS</mark> in adults is not invariably irreversible and that , despite prolonged <mark>oliguria</mark> , recovery of renal function can be obtained . 
Therefore , in adult patients affected by <mark>HUS</mark> , dialysis should not be discontinued prematurely ; moreover , bilateral nephrectomy , for treatment of severe <mark>hypertension</mark> and <mark>microangiopathic hemolytic anemia</mark> , should be performed with caution . 
Morphological features of <mark>encephalopathy</mark> after chronic administration of the antiepileptic drug valproate to rats . 
A transmission electron microscopic study of capillaries in the cerebellar cortex . 
Long - term intragastric application of the antiepileptic drug sodium valproate ( Vupral " Polfa " ) at the effective dose of 200 mg / kg b . 
w . once daily to rats for 1 , 3 , 6 , 9 and 12 months revealed <mark>neurological disorders</mark> indicating <mark>cerebellum damage</mark> ( " valproate <mark>encephalopathy</mark> " ) . 
The first ultrastructural changes in structural elements of the blood - brain - barrier ( BBB ) in the cerebellar cortex were detectable after 3 months of the experiment . 
They became more severe in the later months of the experiment , and were most severe after 12 months , located mainly in the molecular layer of the cerebellar cortex . 
Lesions of the capillary included <mark>necrosis</mark> of endothelial cells . 
Organelles of these cells , in particular the mitochondria ( increased number and size , distinct degeneration of their matrix and cristae ) and Golgi apparatus were altered . 
Reduced size of capillary lumen and occlusion were caused by swollen endothelial cells which had luminal protrusions and swollen microvilli . 
Pressure on the vessel wall was produced by enlarged perivascular astrocytic processes . 
Fragments of <mark>necrotic</mark> endothelial cells were in the vascular lumens and in these there was loosening and breaking of tight cellular junctions . 
Damage to the vascular basement lamina was also observed . 
Damage to the capillary was accompanied by marked damage to neuroglial cells , mainly to perivascular processes of astrocytes . 
The proliferation of astrocytes ( Bergmann ' s in particular ) and occasionally of oligodendrocytes was found . 
Alterations in the structural elements of the BBB coexisted with marked lesions of neurons of the cerebellum ( Purkinje cells are earliest ) . 
In electron micrographs both luminal and antiluminal sides of the BBB of the cerebellar cortex had similar lesions . 
The possible influence of the <mark>hepatic damage</mark> , mainly <mark>hyperammonemia</mark> , upon the development of valproate <mark>encephalopathy</mark> is discussed . 
Fatal <mark>intracranial bleeding</mark> associated with prehospital use of epinephrine . 
We present a case of paramedic misjudgment in the execution of a protocol for the treatment of <mark>allergic reaction</mark> in a case of <mark>pulmonary edema</mark> with <mark>wheezing</mark> . 
The sudden onset of <mark>respiratory distress</mark> , <mark>rash</mark> , and a history of a new medicine led the two paramedics on the scene to administer subcutaneous epinephrine . 
Subsequently , acute <mark>cardiac arrest</mark> and fatal <mark>subarachnoid hemorrhage</mark> occurred . 
Epinephrine has a proven role in <mark>cardiac arrest</mark> in prehospital care ; however , use by paramedics in patients with suspected <mark>allergic reaction</mark> and severe <mark>hypertension</mark> should be viewed with caution . 
Role of activation of bradykinin B2 receptors in disruption of the blood - brain barrier during acute <mark>hypertension</mark> . 
Cellular mechanisms which account for disruption the blood - brain barrier during acute <mark>hypertension</mark> are not clear . 
The goal of this study was to determine the role of synthesis / release of bradykinin to activate B2 receptors in disruption of the blood - brain barrier during acute <mark>hypertension</mark> . 
Permeability of the blood - brain barrier was quantitated by clearance of fluorescent - labeled dextran before and during phenylephrine - induced acute <mark>hypertension</mark> in rats treated with vehicle and Hoe - 140 ( 0 . 1 microM ) . 
Phenylephrine infusion increased arterial pressure , arteriolar diameter and clearance of fluorescent dextran by a similar magnitude in both groups . 
These findings suggest that disruption of the blood - brain barrier during acute <mark>hypertension</mark> is not related to the synthesis / release of bradykinin to activate B2 receptors . 
Risk factors of <mark>sensorineural hearing loss</mark> in preterm infants . 
Among 547 preterm infants of < or = 34 weeks gestation born between 1987 and 1991 , 8 children ( 1 . 46 % ) developed severe progressive and bilateral <mark>sensorineural hearing loss</mark> . 
Perinatal risk factors of infants with <mark>hearing loss</mark> were compared with those of two control groups matched for gestation and birth weight and for perinatal complications . 
Our observations demonstrated an association of <mark>hearing loss</mark> with a higher incidence of perinatal complications . 
<mark>Ototoxicity</mark> appeared closely related to a prolonged administration and higher total dose of <mark>ototoxic</mark> drugs , particularly aminoglycosides and furosemide . 
Finally , we strongly recommend to prospectively and regularly perform audiologic assessment in sick preterm children as <mark>hearing loss</mark> is of delayed onset and in most cases bilateral and severe . 
<mark>Seizure</mark> resulting from a venlafaxine <mark>overdose</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : To report a case of venlafaxine <mark>overdose</mark> . 
CASE SUMMARY : A 40 - year - old woman with <mark>major depression</mark> took an <mark>overdose</mark> of venlafaxine in an apparent suicide attempt . 
After the ingestion of 26 venlafaxine 50 - mg tablets , the patient experienced a witnessed generalized <mark>seizure</mark> . 
She was admitted to the medical intensive care unit , venlafaxine was discontinued , and no further sequelae were seen . 
DISCUSSION : To our knowledge , this is the first reported case of venlafaxine <mark>overdose</mark> that resulted in a generalized <mark>seizure</mark> . 
Based on nonoverdose pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of venlafaxine and the potential risks of available interventions , no emergent therapy was instituted . 
CONCLUSIONS : The venlafaxine <mark>overdose</mark> in our patient resulted in a single episode of generalized <mark>seizure</mark> but elicited no further sequelae . 
Combined effects of prolonged prostaglandin E1 - induced <mark>hypotension</mark> and <mark>haemodilution</mark> on human hepatic function . 
Combined effects of prolonged prostaglandin E1 ( PGE1 ) - induced <mark>hypotension</mark> and <mark>haemodilution</mark> on hepatic function were studied in 30 patients undergoing hip surgery . 
The patients were randomly allocated to one of three groups ; those in group A ( n = 10 ) were subjected to controlled <mark>hypotension</mark> alone , those in group B ( n = 10 ) to <mark>haemodilution</mark> alone and those in group C ( n = 10 ) to both controlled <mark>hypotension</mark> and <mark>haemodilution</mark> . 
<mark>Haemodilution</mark> in groups B and C was produced by withdrawing approximately 1000 mL of blood and replacing it with the same amount of dextran solution , and final haematocrit values were 21 or 22 % . 
Controlled <mark>hypotension</mark> in groups A and C was induced with PGE1 to maintain mean arterial blood pressure at 55 mmHg for 180 min . 
Measurements included arterial ketone body ratio ( AKBR , aceto - acetate / 3 - hydroxybutyrate ) and clinical hepatic function parameters . 
AKBR and biological hepatic function tests showed no change throughout the time course in groups A and B . 
In group C , AKBR showed a significant decrease at 120 min ( - 40 % ) and at 180 min ( - 49 % ) after the start of <mark>hypotension</mark> and at 60 min ( - 32 % ) after recovery of normotension , and SGOT , SGPT , LDH and total bilirubin showed significant increases after operation . 
The results suggest that a prolonged combination of more than 120 min of PGE1 - induced <mark>hypotension</mark> and moderate <mark>haemodilution</mark> would cause <mark>impairment of hepatic function</mark> . 
<mark>Cardiovascular alterations</mark> in rat fetuses exposed to calcium channel blockers . 
Preclinical toxicologic investigation suggested that a new calcium channel blocker , Ro 40 - 5967 , induced <mark>cardiovascular alterations</mark> in rat fetuses exposed to this agent during organogenesis . 
The present study was designed to investigate the hypothesis that calcium channel blockers in general induce <mark>cardiovascular malformations</mark> indicating a pharmacologic class effect . 
We studied three calcium channel blockers of different structure , nifedipine , diltiazem , and verapamil , along with the new agent . 
Pregnant rats were administered one of these calcium channel blockers during the period of cardiac morphogenesis and the offspring examined on day 20 of gestation for <mark>cardiovascular malformations</mark> . 
A low incidence of <mark>cardiovascular malformations</mark> was observed after exposure to each of the four calcium channel blockers , but this incidence was statistically significant only for verapamil and nifedipine . 
All four agents were associated with aortic arch branching variants , although significantly increased only for Ro 40 - 5967 and verapamil . 
The site of common side effects of sumatriptan . 
<mark>Atypical sensations</mark> following the use of subcutaneous sumatriptan are common , but of uncertain origin . 
They are almost always benign , but can be mistaken for a serious adverse event by the patient . 
Two patients are presented with <mark>tingling or burning sensations</mark> limited to areas of heat exposure or <mark>sunburn</mark> . 
In these individuals , side effects are most likely generated superficially in the skin . 
Macula <mark>toxicity</mark> after intravitreal amikacin . 
BACKGROUND : Although intravitreal aminoglycosides have substantially improved visual prognosis in <mark>endophthalmitis</mark> , macular <mark>infarction</mark> may impair full visual recovery . 
METHODS : We present a case of presumed amikacin <mark>retinal toxicity</mark> following treatment with amikacin and vancomycin for alpha - haemolytic <mark>streptococcal endophthalmitis</mark> . 
RESULTS : <mark>Endophthalmitis</mark> resolved with improvement in visual acuity to 6 / 24 at three months . 
Fundus fluorescein angiography confirmed macular capillary closure and <mark>telangiectasis</mark> . 
CONCLUSIONS : Currently accepted intravitreal antibiotic regimens may cause <mark>retinal toxicity</mark> and macular <mark>ischaemia</mark> . 
Treatment strategies aimed at avoiding <mark>retinal toxicity</mark> are discussed . 
The role of nicotine in smoking - related <mark>cardiovascular disease</mark> . 
Nicotine activates the sympathetic nervous system and in this way could contribute to <mark>cardiovascular disease</mark> . 
Animal studies and mechanistic studies indicate that nicotine could play a role in accelerating <mark>atherosclerosis</mark> , but evidence among humans is too inadequate to be definitive about such an effect . 
Almost certainly , nicotine via its hemodynamic effects contributes to acute cardiovascular events , although current evidence suggests that the effects of nicotine are much less important than are the prothrombotic effects of cigarette smoking or the effects of carbon monoxide . 
Nicotine does not appear to enhance <mark>thrombosis</mark> among humans . 
Clinical studies of pipe smokers and people using transdermal nicotine support the idea that toxins other than nicotine are the most important causes of acute cardiovascular events . 
Finally , the dose response for cardiovascular events of nicotine appears to be flat , suggesting that if nicotine is involved , adverse effects might be seen with relatively low - level cigarette exposures . 
Iatrogenically induced intractable <mark>atrioventricular reentrant tachycardia</mark> after verapamil and catheter ablation in a patient with <mark>Wolff - Parkinson - White syndrome</mark> and <mark>idiopathic dilated cardiomyopathy</mark> . 
In a patient with <mark>WPW syndrome</mark> and <mark>idiopathic dilated cardiomyopathy</mark> , intractable <mark>atrioventricular reentrant tachycardia</mark> ( <mark>AVRT</mark> ) was iatrogenically induced . 
QRS without preexcitation , caused by junctional escape beats after verapamil or unidirectional antegrade block of accessory pathway after catheter ablation , established frequent <mark>AVRT</mark> attack . 
Epidemic of <mark>liver disease</mark> caused by hydrochlorofluorocarbons used as ozone - sparing substitutes of chlorofluorocarbons . 
BACKGROUND : Hydrochlorofluorocarbons ( HCFCs ) are used increasingly in industry as substitutes for ozone - depleting chlorofluorocarbons ( CFCs ) . 
Limited studies in animals indicate potential <mark>hepatotoxicity</mark> of some of these compounds . 
We investigated an epidemic of <mark>liver disease</mark> in nine industrial workers who had had repeated accidental exposure to a mixture of 1 , 1 - dichloro - 2 , 2 , 2 - trifluoroethane ( HCFC 123 ) and 1 - chloro - 1 , 2 , 2 , 2 - tetrafluoroethane ( HCFC 124 ) . 
All nine exposed workers were affected to various degrees . 
Both compounds are metabolised in the same way as 1 - bromo - 1 - chloro - 2 , 2 , 2 - trifluoroethane ( halothane ) to form reactive trifluoroacetyl halide intermediates , which have been implicated in the <mark>hepatotoxicity</mark> of halothane . 
We aimed to test whether HCFCs 123 and 124 can result in serious <mark>liver disease</mark> . 
METHODS : For one severely affected worker liver biopsy and immunohistochemical stainings for the presence of trifluoroacetyl protein adducts were done . 
The serum of six affected workers and five controls was tested for autoantibodies that react with human liver cytochrome - P450 2E1 ( P450 2E1 ) and P58 protein disulphide isomerase isoform ( P58 ) . 
FINDINGS : The liver biopsy sample showed hepatocellular <mark>necrosis</mark> which was prominent in perivenular zone three and extended focally from portal tracts to portal tracts and centrilobular areas ( bridging <mark>necrosis</mark> ) . 
Trifluoroacetyl - adducted proteins were detected in surviving hepatocytes . 
Autoantibodies against P450 2E1 or P58 , previously associated with <mark>halothane hepatitis</mark> , were detected in the serum of five affected workers . 
INTERPRETATION : Repeated exposure of human beings to HCFCs 123 and 124 can result in serious <mark>liver injury</mark> in a large proportion of the exposed population . 
Although the exact mechanism of <mark>hepatotoxicity</mark> of these agents is not known , the results suggest that trifluoroacetyl - altered liver proteins are involved . 
In view of the potentially widespread use of these compounds , there is an urgent need to develop safer alternatives . 
<mark>Bile duct hamartoma</mark> occurring in association with long - term treatment with danazol . 
We report a case of <mark>bile duct hamartoma</mark> which developed in a patient who had been on long - term danazol treatment . 
Such patients should be under close follow - up , preferably with periodic ultrasound examination of the liver . 
If the patient develops a <mark>liver mass</mark> , because of non - specific clinical features and imaging appearances , biopsy may be the only way to achieve a definitive diagnosis . 
Endocrine screening in 1 , 022 men with <mark>erectile dysfunction</mark> : clinical significance and cost - effective strategy . 
PURPOSE : We reviewed the results of serum testosterone and prolactin determination in 1 , 022 patients referred because of <mark>erectile dysfunction</mark> and compared the data with history , results of physical examination , other etiological investigations and effects of endocrine therapy to refine the rules of cost - effective endocrine screening and to pinpoint actual responsibility for hormonal abnormalities . 
MATERIALS AND METHODS : Testosterone and prolactin were determined by radioimmunoassay . 
Every patient was screened for testosterone and 451 were screened for prolactin on the basis of <mark>low sexual desire</mark> , <mark>gynecomastia</mark> or testosterone less than 4 ng . / ml . 
Determination was repeated in case of abnormal first results . 
Prolactin results were compared with those of a previous personal cohort of 1 , 340 patients with <mark>erectile dysfunction</mark> and systematic prolactin determination . 
Main clinical criteria tested regarding efficiency in hormone determination were <mark>low sexual desire</mark> , small testes and <mark>gynecomastia</mark> . 
Endocrine therapy consisted of testosterone heptylate or human chorionic gonadotropin for <mark>hypogonadism</mark> and bromocriptine for <mark>hyperprolactinemia</mark> . 
RESULTS : Testosterone was less than 3 ng . / ml . in 107 patients but normal in 40 % at repeat determination . 
The prevalence of repeatedly low testosterone increased with age ( 4 % before age 50 years and 9 % 50 years or older ) . 
Two <mark>pituitary tumors</mark> were discovered after testosterone determination . 
Most of the other low testosterone levels seemed to result from nonorganic <mark>hypothalamic dysfunction</mark> because of normal serum luteinizing hormone and prolactin and to have only a small role in <mark>erectile dysfunction</mark> ( definite improvement in only 16 of 44 [ 36 % ] after androgen therapy , normal morning or nocturnal erections in 30 % and definite vasculogenic contributions in 42 % ) . 
Determining testosterone only in cases of <mark>low sexual desire</mark> or abnormal physical examination would have missed 40 % of the cases with low testosterone , including 37 % of those subsequently improved by androgen therapy . 
Prolactin exceeded 20 ng . / ml . in 5 men and was normal in 2 at repeat determination . 
Only 1 <mark>prolactinoma</mark> was discovered . 
These data are lower than those we found during the last 2 decades ( overall prolactin greater than 20 ng . / ml . in 1 . 86 % of 1 , 821 patients , <mark>prolactinomas</mark> in 7 , 0 . 38 % ) . 
Bromocriptine was definitely effective in cases with prolactin greater than 35 ng . / ml . 
( 8 of 12 compared to only 9 of 22 cases with prolactin between 20 and 35 ng . / ml . ) . 
Testosterone was low in less than 50 % of cases with prolactin greater than 35 ng . / ml . 
CONCLUSIONS : Low prevalences and effects of low testosterone and high prolactin in <mark>erectile dysfunction</mark> cannot justify their routine determination . 
However , cost - effective screening strategies recommended so far missed 40 to 50 % of cases improved with endocrine therapy and the <mark>pituitary tumors</mark> . 
We now advocate that before age 50 years testosterone be determined only in cases of <mark>low sexual desire</mark> and abnormal physical examination but that it be measured in all men older than 50 years . 
Prolactin should be determined only in cases of <mark>low sexual desire</mark> , <mark>gynecomastia</mark> and / or testosterone less than 4 ng . / ml . 
Extrapyramidal side effects with risperidone and haloperidol at comparable D2 receptor occupancy levels . 
Risperidone is an antipsychotic drug with high affinity at dopamine D2 and serotonin 5 - HT2 receptors . 
Previous clinical studies have proposed that risperidone ' s pharmacologic profile may produce improved efficacy for negative <mark>psychotic symptoms</mark> and decreased propensity for extrapyramidal side effects ; features shared by so - called ' atypical ' neuroleptics . 
To determine if routine risperidone treatment is associated with a unique degree of D2 receptor occupancy and pattern of clinical effects , we used [ 123I ] IBZM SPECT to determine D2 occupancy in subjects treated with routine clinical doses of risperidone ( n = 12 ) or haloperidol ( n = 7 ) . 
Both risperidone and haloperidol produced D2 occupancy levels between approximately 60 and 90 % at standard clinical doses . 
There was no significant difference between occupancy levels obtained with haloperidol or risperidone . 
<mark>Drug - induced parkinsonism</mark> was observed in subjects treated with risperidone ( 42 % ) and haloperidol ( 29 % ) and was observed at occupancy levels above 60 % . 
Based on these observations , it is concluded that 5 - HT2 blockade obtained with risperidone at D2 occupancy rates of 60 % and above does not appear to protect against the risk for extrapyramidal side effects . 
Treatment of previously treated metastatic <mark>breast cancer</mark> by mitoxantrone and 48 - hour continuous infusion of high - dose 5 - FU and leucovorin ( MFL ) : low palliative benefit and high treatment - related <mark>toxicity</mark> . 
For previously treated advanced <mark>breast cancer</mark> , there is no standard second - line therapy . 
Combination chemotherapy with mitoxantrone , high - dose 5 - fluorouracil ( 5 - FU ) and leucovorin ( MFL regimen ) had been reported as an effective and well tolerated regimen . 
From October 1993 to November 1995 , we treated 13 patients with previously chemotherapy - treated metastatic <mark>breast cancer</mark> by mitoxantrone , 12 mg / m2 , on day 1 and continuous infusion of 5 - FU , 3000 mg / m2 , together with leucovorin , 300 mg / m2 , for 48 h from day 1 to 2 . 
Each course of chemotherapy was given every 4 weeks . 
Most of these patients had more than two metastatic sites , with lung metastasis predominant . 
Seven patients had been treated with anthracycline . 
Seven patients had previously received radiotherapy and seven had received hormone therapy . 
Median number of courses of MFL regimen given was six and the median cumulative dose of mitoxantrone was 68 . 35 mg / m2 . 
One patient had complete response , seven had stable disease , none had partial response and five had progressive disease . 
The overall objective response rate was 7 . 6 % . 
The median follow - up period was 14 months . 
Median survival was 16 months . 
Median progression - free survival was 5 months . 
A complete responder had relapse - free survival up to 17 months . 
Major <mark>toxicities</mark> were <mark>cardiotoxicity</mark> and <mark>leukopenia</mark> . 
Eight patients were dead in the last follow - up ; two of them died of treatment - related <mark>toxicity</mark> . 
The MFL regimen achieves little palliative benefit and induces severe <mark>toxicity</mark> at a fairly high rate . 
Administration of this regimen to <mark>breast cancer</mark> patients who have been treated by chemotherapy and those with <mark>impaired heart function</mark> requires careful attention . 
Ticlopidine - induced <mark>aplastic anemia</mark> : report of three Chinese patients and review of the literature . 
In this study , three Chinese patients with ticlopidine - induced <mark>aplastic anemia</mark> were reported and another 13 patients in the English literature were reviewed . 
We attempted to find underlying similarities , evaluate the risk factors , and identify appropriate treatment for this complication . 
All but one of the patients were over 60 years old , and the 6 who died were all older than 65 . 
Therefore , old age may be a risk factor for developing this complication . 
<mark>Agranulocytosis</mark> occurred 3 - 20 weeks after initiation of ticlopidine , so frequent examination of white cell count during treatment is recommended . 
There seemed to be no direct correlation between the dose or duration used and the severity of <mark>bone marrow suppression</mark> . 
Treatment for ticlopidine - induced <mark>aplastic anemia</mark> with colony - stimulating factors seemed to have little effect . 
The fact that 5 of the 6 patients who received concurrent calcium channel blockers died , should alert clinicians to be more cautious when using these two drugs simultaneously . 
Upregulation of the expression of vasopressin gene in the paraventricular and supraoptic nuclei of the lithium - induced <mark>diabetes insipidus</mark> rat . 
The expression of arginine vasopressin ( AVP ) gene in the paraventricular ( PVN ) and supraoptic nuclei ( SON ) was investigated in rats with lithium ( Li ) - induced <mark>polyuria</mark> , using in situ hybridization histochemistry and radioimmunoassay . 
The male Wistar rats consuming a diet that contained LiCl ( 60 mmol / kg ) for 4 weeks developed marked <mark>polyuria</mark> . 
The Li - treated rats produced a large volume of hypotonic urine with low ionic concentrations . 
Plasma sodium concentrations were found to be slightly increased in the Li - treated rats compared with those in controls . 
Plasma concentration of AVP and transcripts of AVP gene in the PVN and SON were significantly increased in the Li - treated rats compared with controls . 
These results suggest that <mark>dehydration</mark> and / or the activation of visceral afferent inputs may contribute to the elevation of plasma AVP and the upregulation of AVP gene expression in the PVN and the SON of the Li - induced <mark>diabetes insipidus</mark> rat . 
Antinociceptive and antiamnesic properties of the presynaptic cholinergic amplifier PG - 9 . 
The antinociceptive effect of 3 alpha - tropyl 2 - ( p - bromophenyl ) propionate [ ( + / - ) - PG - 9 ] ( 10 - 40 mg kg - 1 s . c . ; 30 - 60 mg kg - 1 p . o . ; 10 - 30 mg kg - 1 i . v . ; 10 - 30 micrograms / mouse i . c . v . ) was examined in mice , rats and guinea pigs by use of the hot - plate , abdominal - constriction , tail - flick and paw - pressure tests . 
( + / - ) - PG - 9 antinociception peaked 15 min after injection and then slowly diminished . 
The antinociception produced by ( + / - ) - PG - 9 was prevented by the unselective muscarinic antagonist atropine , the M1 - selective antagonists pirenzepine and dicyclomine and the acetylcholine depletor hemicholinium - 3 , but not by the opioid antagonist naloxone , the gamma - aminobutyric acidB antagonist 3 - aminopropyl - diethoxy - methyl - phosphinic acid , the H3 agonist R - ( alpha ) - methylhistamine , the D2 antagonist quinpirole , the 5 - hydroxytryptamine4 antagonist 2 - methoxy - 4 - amino - 5 - chlorobenzoic acid 2 - ( diethylamino ) ethyl ester hydrochloride , the 5 - hydroxytryptamin1A antagonist 1 - ( 2 - methoxyphenyl ) - 4 - [ 4 - ( 2 - phthalimido ) butyl ] piperazine hydrobromide and the polyamines depletor reserpine . 
Based on these data , it can be postulated that ( + / - ) - PG - 9 exerted an antinociceptive effect mediated by a central potentiation of cholinergic transmission . 
( + / - ) - PG - 9 ( 10 - 40 mg kg - 1 i . p . ) was able to prevent <mark>amnesia</mark> induced by scopolamine ( 1 mg kg - 1 i . p . ) and dicyclomine ( 2 mg kg - 1 i . p . ) in the mouse passive - avoidance test . 
Affinity profiles of ( + / - ) - PG - 9 for muscarinic receptor subtypes , determined by functional studies ( rabbit vas deferens for M1 , guinea pig atrium for M2 , guinea pig ileum for M3 and immature guinea pig uterus for putative M4 ) , have shown an M4 / M1 selectivity ratio of 10 . 2 that might be responsible for the antinociception and the anti - <mark>amnesic</mark> effect induced by ( + / - ) - PG - 9 through an increase in acetylcholine extracellular levels . 
In the antinociceptive and antiamnesic dose range , ( + / - ) - PG - 9 did not impair mouse performance evaluated by the rota - rod test and Animex apparatus . 
The effect of different anaesthetic agents in <mark>hearing loss</mark> following spinal anaesthesia . 
The cause of <mark>hearing loss</mark> after spinal anaesthesia is unknown . 
Up until now , the only factor studied has been the effect of the diameter of the spinal needle on post - operative <mark>sensorineural hearing loss</mark> . 
The aim of this study was to describe this <mark>hearing loss</mark> and to investigate other factors influencing the degree of <mark>hearing loss</mark> . 
Two groups of 22 similar patients were studied : one group received 6 mL prilocaine 2 % ; and the other received 3 mL bupivacaine 0 . 5 % . 
Patients given prilocaine were more likely to develop <mark>hearing loss</mark> ( 10 out of 22 ) than those given bupivacaine ( 4 out of 22 ) ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 
The average <mark>hearing loss</mark> for speech frequencies was about 10 dB after prilocaine and 15 dB after bupivacaine . 
None of the patients complained of subjective <mark>hearing loss</mark> . 
Long - term follow - up of the patients was not possible . 
A transient <mark>neurological deficit</mark> following intrathecal injection of 1 % hyperbaric bupivacaine for unilateral spinal anaesthesia . 
We describe a case of transient <mark>neurological deficit</mark> that occurred after unilateral spinal anaesthesia with 8 mg of 1 % hyperbaric bupivacaine slowly injected through a 25 - gauge pencil - point spinal needle . 
The surgery and anaesthesia were uneventful , but 3 days after surgery , the patient reported an area of hypoaesthesia over L3 - L4 dermatomes of the leg which had been operated on ( <mark>loss of pinprick sensation</mark> ) without reduction in muscular strength . 
Sensation in this area returned to normal over the following 2 weeks . 
Prospective multicentre studies with a large population and a long follow - up should be performed in order to evaluate the incidence of this unusual side effect . 
However , we suggest that a low solution concentration should be preferred for unilateral spinal anaesthesia with a hyperbaric anaesthetic solution ( if pencil - point needle and slow injection rate are employed ) , in order to minimize the risk of a localized high peak anaesthetic concentration , which might lead to a transient <mark>neurological deficit</mark> . 
<mark>Transient neurologic symptoms</mark> after spinal anesthesia : a lower incidence with prilocaine and bupivacaine than with lidocaine . 
BACKGROUND : Recent evidence suggests that <mark>transient neurologic symptoms</mark> ( <mark>TNSs</mark> ) frequently follow lidocaine spinal anesthesia but are infrequent with bupivacaine . 
However , identification of a short - acting local anesthetic to substitute for lidocaine for brief surgical procedures remains an important goal . 
Prilocaine is an amide local anesthetic with a duration of action similar to that of lidocaine . 
Accordingly , the present , prospective double - blind study compares prilocaine with lidocaine and bupivacaine with respect to duration of action and relative risk of <mark>TNSs</mark> . 
METHODS : Ninety patients classified as American Society of Anesthesiologists physical status I or II who were scheduled for short gynecologic procedures under spinal anesthesia were randomly allocated to receive 2 . 5 ml 2 % lidocaine in 7 . 5 % glucose , 2 % prilocaine in 7 . 5 % glucose , or 0 . 5 % bupivacaine in 7 . 5 % glucose . 
All solutions were provided in blinded vials by the hospital pharmacy . 
Details of spinal puncture , extension and regression of spinal block , and the times to reach discharge criteria were noted . 
In the evening of postoperative day 1 , patients were evaluated for <mark>TNSs</mark> by a physician unaware of the drug administered and the details of the anesthetic procedure . 
RESULTS : Nine of 30 patients receiving lidocaine experienced <mark>TNSs</mark> , 1 of 30 patients receiving prilocaine ( P = 0 . 03 ) had them , and none of 30 patients receiving bupivacaine had <mark>TNSs</mark> . 
Times to ambulate and to void were similar after lidocaine and prilocaine ( 150 vs . 165 min and 238 vs . 253 min , respectively ) but prolonged after bupivacaine ( 200 and 299 min , respectively ; P < 0 . 05 ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : Prilocaine may be preferable to lidocaine for short surgical procedures because it has a similar duration of action but a lower incidence of <mark>TNSs</mark> . 
Suxamethonium - induced <mark>cardiac arrest</mark> and <mark>death</mark> following 5 days of immobilization . 
The present report describes a case of <mark>cardiac arrest</mark> and subsequent <mark>death</mark> as a result of <mark>hyperkalaemia</mark> following the use of suxamethonium in a 23 - year - old Malawian woman . 
Five days after the onset of the symptoms of <mark>meningitis</mark> , the patient aspirated stomach contents and needed endotracheal intubation . 
Forty seconds after injection of suxamethonium , <mark>bradycardia</mark> and <mark>cardiac arrest</mark> occurred . 
Attempts to resuscitate the patient were not successful . 
The serum level of potassium was observed to be 8 . 4 mequiv L - 1 . 
Apart from the reduction in the patient ' s level of consciousness , there were no signs of motor neurone damage or of any of the other known predisposing conditions for <mark>hyperkalaemia</mark> following the administration of suxamethonium . 
It is postulated that her <mark>death</mark> was caused by <mark>hypersensitivity</mark> to suxamethonium , associated with her 5 - day immobilization . 
Acute <mark>hepatitis</mark> , <mark>autoimmune hemolytic anemia</mark> , and <mark>erythroblastocytopenia</mark> induced by ceftriaxone . 
An 80 - yr - old man developed acute <mark>hepatitis</mark> shortly after ingesting oral ceftriaxone . 
Although the transaminases gradually returned to baseline after withholding the beta lactam antibiotic , there was a gradual increase in serum bilirubin and a decrease in hemoglobin concentration caused by an <mark>autoimmune hemolytic anemia</mark> and <mark>erythroblastocytopenia</mark> . 
These responded to systemic steroids and immunoglobulins . 
Despite the widespread use of these agents this triad of side effects has not previously been reported in connection with beta lactam antibiotics . 
Thyroxine abuse : an unusual case of <mark>thyrotoxicosis</mark> in pregnancy . 
<mark>Eating disorders</mark> and the associated behavioural problems and <mark>drug abuse</mark> are uncommon in pregnancy . 
When they do occur they are often unrecognized because of denial but when significant may pose a risk to both the mother and her fetus . 
This case illustrates a number of problems that may be encountered in women with <mark>eating disorders</mark> in pregnancy , including prolonged and recurrent metabolic disturbances and diuretic abuse . 
In particular it illustrates the derangements of thyroid function seen in pregnant women with <mark>eating disorders</mark> and reminds us that when a cause for <mark>thyrotoxicosis</mark> remains obscure , thyroxine abuse should be considered and explored . 
Repeated trimipramine induces dopamine D2 / D3 and alpha1 - adrenergic up - regulation . 
Trimipramine ( TRI ) , which shows a clinical antidepressant activity , is chemically related to imipramine but does not inhibit the reuptake of noradrenaline and 5 - hydroxytryptamine , nor does it induce beta - adrenergic down - regulation . 
The mechanism of its antidepressant activity is still unknown . 
The aim of the present study was to find out whether TRI given repeatedly was able to induce adaptive changes in the dopaminergic and alpha1 - adrenergic systems , demonstrated by us previously for various antidepressants . 
TRI was given to male Wistar rats and male Albino Swiss mice perorally twice daily for 14 days . 
In the acute experiment TRI ( given i . p . ) does not antagonize the reserpine <mark>hypothermia</mark> in mice and does not potentiate the 5 - hydroxytryptophan head twitches in rats . 
TRI given repeatedly to rats increases the locomotor <mark>hyperactivity</mark> induced by d - amphetamine , quinpirole and ( + ) - 7 - hydroxy - dipropyloaminotetralin ( dopamine D2 and D3 effects ) . 
The stereotypies induced by d - amphetamine or apomorphine are not potentiated by TRI . 
It increases the behaviour stimulation evoked by phenylephrine ( given intraventricularly ) in rats , evaluated in the open field test as well as the <mark>aggressiveness</mark> evoked by clonidine in mice , both these effects being mediated by an alpha1 - adrenergic receptor . 
It may be concluded that , like other tricyclic antidepressants studied previously , TRI given repeatedly increases the responsiveness of brain dopamine D2 and D3 ( locomotor activity but not stereotypy ) as well as alpha1 - adrenergic receptors to their agonists . 
A question arises whether the reuptake inhibition is of any importance to the adaptive changes induced by repeated antidepressants , suggested to be responsible for the antidepressant activity . 
Pethidine - associated <mark>seizure</mark> in a healthy adolescent receiving pethidine for <mark>postoperative pain</mark> control . 
A healthy 17 - year - old male received standard intermittent doses of pethidine via a patient - controlled analgesia ( PCA ) pump for management of <mark>postoperative pain</mark> control . 
Twenty - three h postoperatively he developed a brief self - limited <mark>seizure</mark> . 
Both plasma pethidine and norpethidine were elevated in the range associated with clinical manifestations of central nervous system excitation . 
No other risk factors for CNS <mark>toxicity</mark> were identified . 
This method allowed frequent self - dosing of pethidine at short time intervals and rapid accumulation of pethidine and norpethidine . 
The routine use of pethidine via PCA even for a brief postoperative analgesia should be reconsidered . 
An unusual toxic reaction to axillary block by mepivacaine with adrenaline .
