An <mark>increase in blood pressure</mark> , accompanied by <mark>atrial fibrillation</mark> , <mark>agitation</mark> , <mark>incomprehensible shouts</mark> and <mark>loss of consciousness</mark> , was observed in an elderly , ASA classification group II , cardiovascularly medicated male , 12 min after performance of axillary block with mepivacaine 850 mg containing adrenaline 0 . 225 mg , for correction of <mark>Dupuytren ' s contracture</mark> . 
After intravenous administration of labetalol , metoprolol and midazolam the patient ' s condition improved , and 15 min later he woke up . 
The block was successful and surgery was conducted as scheduled despite persisting <mark>atrial fibrillation</mark> . 
Postoperatively , the patient refused DC cardioversion and was treated medically . 
Both the temporal relationship of events and the response to treatment suggest that a rapid systemic absorption of mepivacaine with adrenaline and / or interaction of these drugs with the patient ' s cardiovascular medications were responsible for the perioperative complications . 
Drug - associated acute - onset <mark>vanishing bile duct</mark> and <mark>Stevens - Johnson syndromes</mark> in a child . 
Acute <mark>vanishing bile duct</mark> syndrome is a rare but established cause of progressive <mark>cholestasis</mark> in adults , is most often drug or toxin related , and is of unknown pathogenesis . 
It has not been reported previously in children . 
<mark>Stevens - Johnson syndrome</mark> is a well - recognized immune complex - mediated <mark>hypersensitivity</mark> reaction that affects all age groups , is drug or <mark>infection</mark> induced , and has classic systemic , mucosal , and dermatologic manifestations . 
A previously healthy child who developed acute , severe , rapidly progressive <mark>vanishing bile duct syndrome</mark> shortly after <mark>Stevens - Johnson syndrome</mark> is described ; this was temporally associated with ibuprofen use . 
Despite therapy with ursodeoxycholic acid , prednisone , and then tacrolimus , her <mark>cholestatic disease</mark> was unrelenting , with <mark>cirrhosis</mark> shown by biopsy 6 months after presentation . 
This case documents acute drug - related <mark>vanishing bile duct syndrome</mark> in the pediatric age group and suggests shared immune mechanisms in the pathogenesis of both <mark>Stevens - Johnson syndrome</mark> and <mark>vanishing bile duct syndrome</mark> . 
High incidence of <mark>primary pulmonary hypertension</mark> associated with appetite suppressants in Belgium . 
<mark>Primary pulmonary hypertension</mark> is a rare , progressive and incurable disease , which has been associated with the intake of appetite suppressant drugs . 
The importance of this association was evaluated in Belgium while this country still had no restriction on the prescription of appetite suppressants . 
Thirty - five patients with <mark>primary pulmonary hypertension</mark> and 85 matched controls were recruited over 32 months ( 1992 - 1994 ) in Belgium . 
Exposure to appetite - suppressants was assessed on the basis of hospital records and standardized interview . 
Twenty - three of the patients had previously taken appetite suppressants , mainly fenfluramines , as compared with only 5 of the controls ( 66 versus 6 % , p < 0 . 0001 ) . 
Five patients died before the interview , all of them had taken appetite suppressants . 
In 8 patients the diagnosis of <mark>primary pulmonary hypertension</mark> was uncertain , 5 of them had taken appetite suppressants . 
The patients who had been exposed to appetite suppressants tended to be on average more severely ill , and to have a shorter median delay between onset of symptoms and diagnosis . 
A policy of unrestricted prescription of appetite suppressants may lead to a high incidence of associated <mark>primary pulmonary hypertension</mark> . 
Intake of appetite suppressants may accelerate the progression of the disease . 
Inappropriate use of carbamazepine and vigabatrin in typical <mark>absence seizures</mark> . 
Carbamazepine and vigabatrin are contraindicated in typical <mark>absence seizures</mark> . 
Of 18 consecutive referrals of children with resistant typical absences only , eight were erroneously treated with carbamazepine either as monotherapy or as an add - on . 
Vigabatrin was also used in the treatment of two children . 
Frequency of absences increased in four children treated with carbamazepine and two of these developed <mark>myoclonic jerks</mark> , which resolved on withdrawal of carbamazepine . 
Absences were aggravated in both cases where vigabatrin was added on to concurrent treatment . 
Optimal control of the absences was achieved with sodium valproate , lamotrigine , or ethosuximide alone or in combination . 
<mark>Choreoathetoid movements</mark> associated with rapid adjustment to methadone . 
<mark>Choreatiform hyperkinesias</mark> are known to be occasional <mark>movement abnormalities</mark> during intoxications with cocaine but not opiates . 
This is a case report of euphoria and <mark>choreoathetoid movements</mark> both transiently induced by rapid adjustment to the selective mu - opioid receptor agonist methadone in an inpatient previously abusing heroine and cocaine . 
In addition , minor EEG abnormalities occurred . 
Possible underlying neurobiological phenomena are discussed . 
Adverse effects of the atypical antipsychotics . 
Collaborative Working Group on Clinical Trial Evaluations . 
Adverse effects of antipsychotics often lead to noncompliance . 
Thus , clinicians should address patients ' concerns about adverse effects and attempt to choose medications that will improve their patients ' quality of life as well as overall health . 
The side effect profiles of the atypical antipsychotics are more advantageous than those of the conventional neuroleptics . 
Conventional agents are associated with unwanted central nervous system effects , including <mark>extrapyramidal symptoms</mark> ( <mark>EPS</mark> ) , <mark>tardive dyskinesia</mark> , sedation , and possible impairment of some cognitive measures , as well as cardiac effects , <mark>orthostatic hypotension</mark> , hepatic changes , anticholinergic side effects , <mark>sexual dysfunction</mark> , and <mark>weight gain</mark> . 
The newer atypical agents have a lower risk of <mark>EPS</mark> , but are associated in varying degrees with sedation , cardiovascular effects , anticholinergic effects , <mark>weight gain</mark> , <mark>sexual dysfunction</mark> , hepatic effects , lowered <mark>seizure</mark> threshold ( primarily clozapine ) , and <mark>agranulocytosis</mark> ( clozapine only ) . 
Since the incidence and severity of specific adverse effects differ among the various atypicals , the clinician should carefully consider which side effects are most likely to lead to the individual ' s dissatisfaction and noncompliance before choosing an antipsychotic for a particular patient . 
A randomized , placebo - controlled dose - comparison trial of haloperidol for <mark>psychosis</mark> and <mark>disruptive behaviors</mark> in <mark>Alzheimer ' s disease</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : The goal of this study was to compare the efficacy and side effects of two doses of haloperidol and placebo in the treatment of <mark>psychosis</mark> and <mark>disruptive behaviors</mark> in patients with <mark>Alzheimer ' s disease</mark> . 
METHOD : In a 6 - week random - assignment , double - blind , placebo - controlled trial ( phase A ) , haloperidol , 2 - 3 mg / day ( standard dose ) , and haloperidol , 0 . 50 - 0 . 75 mg / day ( low dose ) , were compared in 71 outpatients with <mark>Alzheimer ' s disease</mark> . 
For the subsequent 6 - week double - blind crossover phase ( phase B ) , patients taking standard - or low - dose haloperidol were switched to placebo , and patients taking placebo were randomly assigned to standard - or low - dose haloperidol . 
RESULTS : For the 60 patients who completed phase A , standard - dose haloperidol was efficacious and superior to both low - dose haloperidol and placebo for scores on the Brief Psychiatric Rating Scale <mark>psychosis</mark> factor and on <mark>psychomotor agitation</mark> . 
Response rates according to three sets of criteria were greater with the standard dose ( 55 % - 60 % ) than the low dose ( 25 % - 35 % ) and placebo ( 25 % - 30 % ) . 
The advantage of standard dose over low dose was replicated in phase B . 
In phase A , <mark>extrapyramidal signs</mark> tended to be greater with the standard dose than in the other two conditions , primarily because of a subgroup ( 20 % ) who developed moderate to severe signs . 
Low - dose haloperidol did not differ from placebo on any measure of efficacy or side effects . 
CONCLUSIONS : The results indicated a favorable therapeutic profile for haloperidol in doses of 2 - 3 mg / day , although a subgroup developed moderate to severe <mark>extrapyramidal signs</mark> . 
A starting dose of 1 mg / day with gradual , upward dose titration is recommended . 
The narrow therapeutic window observed with haloperidol may also apply to other neuroleptics used in <mark>Alzheimer ' s disease</mark> patients with <mark>psychosis</mark> and <mark>disruptive behaviors</mark> . 
Effects of acetylsalicylic acid , dipyridamole , and hydrocortisone on epinephrine - induced <mark>myocardial injury</mark> in dogs . 
A reproducible model for producing diffuse <mark>myocardial injury</mark> ( epinephrine infusion ) has been developed to study the cardioprotective effects of agents or maneuvers which might alter the evolution of acute <mark>myocardial infarction</mark> . 
Infusions of epinephrine ( 4 mug per kilogram per minute for 6 hours ) increased radiocalcium uptakes into intact myocardium and each of its subcellular components with the mitochondrial fraction showing the most consistent changes when compared to saline - infused control animals ( 4 , 957 vs . 827 counts per minute per gram of dried tissue or fraction ) . 
Myocardial concentrations of calcium also increased significantly ( 12 . 0 vs . 5 . 0 mg . per 100 Gm . of fat - free dry weight ) . 
Infusions of calcium chloride sufficient to raise serum calcium concentrations 2 mEq . per liter failed to increase calcium influx into the myocardial cell . 
Mitochondrial radiocalcium uptakes were significantly decreased in animals pretreated with acetylsalicylic acid or dipyridamole or when hydrocortisone was added to the epinephrine infusion ( 2 , 682 , 2 , 803 , and 3 , 424 counts per minute per gram of dried fraction , respectively ) . 
Myocardial calcium concentrations also were decreased ( 11 . 2 , 8 . 3 , and 8 . 9 mg . per 100 Gm . of fat - free dry weight , respectively ) in the three treatment groups , being significantly decreased only in the last two . 
Evidence of microscopic damage was graded as less severe in the three treatment groups . 
Acetylsalicylic acid , dipyridamole , and hydrocortisone all appear to have cardioprotective effects when tested in this model . 
Clinical and histopathologic examination of renal allografts treated with tacrolimus ( FK506 ) for at least one year . 
BACKGROUND : We clinically and pathologically analyzed renal allografts from 1 9 renal transplant patients treated with tacrolimus ( FK506 ) for more than 1 year . 
METHODS : Twenty - six renal allograft biopsy specimens from 1 9 renal transplant patients who underwent transplantations between 1991 and 1993 were evaluated . 
Thirteen biopsies were performed from stable functioning renal allografts with informed consent ( nonepisode biopsy ) and the other 13 were from dysfunctional renal allografts with a clinical indication for biopsy ( episode biopsy ) . 
RESULTS : The main pathologic diagnoses ( some overlap ) were acute rejection ( AR ; n = 4 ) , chronic rejection ( CR ; n = 5 ) , AR + CR ( n = 4 ) , recurrent <mark>IgA nephropathy</mark> ( n = 5 ) , normal findings ( n = 2 ) , minimal - type chronic FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> ( n = 9 ) , and mild - type FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> ( n = 11 ) . 
Of the nonepisode biopsies , 7 and 4 biopsies showed minimal - type and mild - type chronic FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> , respectively . 
Chronic FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> consisted of rough and foamy tubular vacuolization ( 5 biopsies ) , arteriolopathy ( angiodegeneration of the arteriolar wall ; 20 biopsies ) , <mark>focal segmental glomerulosclerosis</mark> ( 4 biopsies ) and the striped form of <mark>interstitial fibrosis</mark> ( 11 biopsies ) . 
The serum creatinine levels of patients in the mild - type chronic FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> group , which included 7 episode biopsies , were statistically higher than those in the minimum - type chronic FK506 - <mark>nephropathy</mark> group ( P < 0 . 001 ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : This study demonstrates that chronic FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> consists primarily of arteriolopathy manifesting as insudative hyalinosis of the arteriolar wall , and suggests that mild - type chronic FK506 <mark>nephropathy</mark> is a condition which may lead to deterioration of renal allograft function . 
Different lobular distributions of altered hepatocyte tight junctions in rat models of <mark>intrahepatic and extrahepatic cholestasis</mark> . 
Hepatocyte tight junctions ( TJs ) , the only intercellular barrier between the sinusoidal and the canalicular spaces , play a key role in bile formation . 
Although hepatocyte TJs are impaired in <mark>cholestasis</mark> , attempts to localize the precise site of hepatocyte TJ damage by freeze - fracture electron microscopy have produced limited information . 
Recently , several TJ - associated proteins like ZO - 1 and 7H6 have been identified and characterized . 
Immunolocalization of 7H6 appears to closely correlate with paracellular permeability . 
We used rat models of <mark>intrahepatic cholestasis</mark> by ethinyl estradiol ( EE ) treatment and <mark>extrahepatic cholestasis</mark> by bile duct ligation ( BDL ) to precisely determine the site of TJ damage . 
Alterations in hepatocyte TJs were assessed by double - immunolabeling for 7H6 and ZO - 1 using a confocal laser scanning microscope . 
In control rats , immunostaining for 7H6 and ZO - 1 colocalized to outline bile canaliculi in a continuous fashion . 
In contrast , 7H6 and ZO - 1 immunostaining was more discontinuous , outlining the bile canaliculi after BDL . 
Immunostaining for 7H6 , not ZO - 1 , decreased and predominantly appeared as discrete signals in the submembranous cytoplasm of periportal hepatocytes after BDL . 
After EE treatment , changes in immunostaining for 7H6 and ZO - 1 were similar to those seen in periportal hepatocytes after BDL , but distributed more diffusely throughout the lobule . 
This study is the first to demonstrate that impairment of hepatocyte TJs occurs heterogenously in the liver lobule after BDL and suggests that BDL and EE treatments produce different lobular distributions of increased paracellular permeability . 
Memory facilitation and stimulation of endogenous nerve growth factor synthesis by the acetylcholine releaser PG - 9 . 
The effects of PG - 9 ( 3alpha - tropyl 2 - ( p - bromophenyl ) propionate ) , the acetylcholine releaser , on memory processes and nerve growth factor ( NGF ) synthesis were evaluated . 
In the mouse passive - avoidance test , PG - 9 ( 10 - 30 mg / kg , i . p . ) , administered 20 min before the training session , prevented <mark>amnesia</mark> induced by both the non selective antimuscarinic drug scopolamine and the M1 - selective antagonist S - ( - ) - ET - 126 . 
In the same experimental conditions , PG - 9 ( 5 - 20 microg per mouse , i . c . v . ) was also able to prevent antimuscarine - induced <mark>amnesia</mark> , demonstrating a central localization of the activity . 
At the highest effective doses , PG - 9 did not produce any collateral symptoms as revealed by the Irwin test , and it did not modify spontaneous motility and inspection activity , as revealed by the hole - board test . 
PG - 9 was also able to increase the amount of NGF secreted in vitro by astrocytes in a dose - dependent manner . 
The maximal NGF contents obtained by PG - 9 were 17 . 6 - fold of the control value . 
During culture , no morphological changes were found at effective concentrations of PG - 9 . 
The current work indicates the ability of PG - 9 to induce beneficial effects on cognitive processes and stimulate activity of NGF synthesis in astroglial cells . 
Therefore , PG - 9 could represent a potential useful drug able to improve the function of impaired cognitive processes . 
Mechanisms of FK 506 - induced <mark>hypertension</mark> in the rat . 
- Tacrolimus ( FK 506 ) is a powerful , widely used immunosuppressant . 
The clinical utility of FK 506 is complicated by substantial <mark>hypertension</mark> and <mark>nephrotoxicity</mark> . 
To clarify the mechanisms of FK 506 - induced <mark>hypertension</mark> , we studied the chronic effects of FK 506 on the synthesis of endothelin - 1 ( ET - 1 ) , the expression of mRNA of ET - 1 and endothelin - converting enzyme - 1 ( ECE - 1 ) , the endothelial nitric oxide synthase ( eNOS ) activity , and the expression of mRNA of eNOS and C - type natriuretic peptide ( CNP ) in rat blood vessels . 
In addition , the effect of the specific endothelin type A receptor antagonist FR 139317 on FK 506 - induced <mark>hypertension</mark> in rats was studied . 
FK 506 , 5 mg . 
kg - 1 . 
d - 1 given for 4 weeks , elevated blood pressure from 102 + / - 13 to 152 + / - 15 mm Hg and increased the synthesis of ET - 1 and the levels of ET - 1 mRNA in the mesenteric artery ( 240 % and 230 % , respectively ) . 
Little change was observed in the expression of ECE - 1 mRNA and CNP mRNA . 
FK 506 decreased eNOS activity and the levels of eNOS mRNA in the aorta ( 48 % and 55 % , respectively ) . 
The administration of FR 139317 ( 10 mg . kg - 1 . d - 1 ) prevented FK 506 - induced <mark>hypertension</mark> in rats . 
These results indicate that FK 506 may increase blood pressure not only by increasing ET - 1 production but also by decreasing NO synthesis in the vasculature .
